    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_453136304" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/453136304" />
    <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie"><img alt="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514769932p2/3275325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/453136304?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie">Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101623503" href="/book/show/17280472-down-london-road">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=emotional-angsty-books">emotional-angsty-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer453136304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1906844678059608349"><b><i>"You know, the world will always try to make you into who it wants you to be. People, time, events, they’ll all try to carve away at you and make you think you don’t know who you are. But it doesn’t matter who they try to make you, or what name they try to give you. If you stay true, you can chip off all their machinations and you’re still you underneath it all.</i> <u>Be Caledonia."</u></b><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379791513i/551243.png' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>That quote epitomizes the book for me and even if you haven't read the book, try to keep it in mind because there are som</span>
  <span id="freeText1906844678059608349" style="display:none"><b><i>"You know, the world will always try to make you into who it wants you to be. People, time, events, they’ll all try to carve away at you and make you think you don’t know who you are. But it doesn’t matter who they try to make you, or what name they try to give you. If you stay true, you can chip off all their machinations and you’re still you underneath it all.</i> <u>Be Caledonia."</u></b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379791513i/551243.png" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>That quote epitomizes the book for me and even if you haven't read the book, try to keep it in mind because there are some things you may not like. <br><br>♦ <u>You may not like:</u> Jo (Johanna). Well, actually, you may not like her from <i>On Dublin Road</i> and if that's the case, you're really not going to like her here...at least until you're past the fifty percent mark then maybe she has a chance. <br><br>♦ <u>You may not like:</u> Cam (Cameron). You will probably think he's hot but there are certain things he does and says that are not very appealing....even after the fifty percent mark. <br><br>♦ <u>You definitely will not like:</u> Jo's mom (Fiona). She's got some problems to say the least. <br><br>♦ <u>You may not like:</u> some of the themes in this book. They don't give you the warm fuzzies. Consequently, some of the characters are messed up...<i>just like real life.</i><br><br>♦ <u>You may not like:</u> the book and you'll give up and not finish. And that's okay. <br><br><b>But</b>...I hope you'll stick it out and give it a chance. There are sooo many things <i>to</i> like. <br><br>♥ <u>I hope you'll like:</u> Cole (Johanna's wee brother). How could you not? Definitely a hottie in the making.<br><br>♥ <u>I hope you'll like:</u> Jo...after the fifty percent mark. She does change and come into her own "Caledonia."<br><br>♥ <u>I hope you'll like:</u> Cam. Okay...we all make mistakes and while there are reasons for some, he does see the error of his ways and makes changes. That has to account for something. <br><br>♥ <u>I hope you'll like:</u> The hot, steamy scenes...yep, there's some good ones especially the dressing room! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/502667.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>♥ <u>I hope you'll like:</u> Mick (Johanna and Cole's "Uncle"). Definitely someone they needed in their life and someone who has their backs. <br><br>♥ <u>I hope you'll like:</u> Joss and Braden. Yes...we gets lots of great moments between the two of them and I love how they <i>both</i> care about Jo. <br><br><b>
  <i>"Some people are born with family, and others have to make family."</i>
</b> (I love that!) <br><br>♥ <u>I hope you'll like:</u> the important theme which is about people liking you for who you are. Not trying to change you but being there for you, supporting you, making you stronger and above everything else...loving you. ♥<br><br>♦ <u>My Thoughts:</u> Obviously, I really enjoyed the book. The first half was hard to get through. Both Jo and Cam are in other relationships and I understand a lot of people don't like that. Was it crucial for the story? Yes. Could it have been shorter? Definitely. I think it would have flowed much better if that part was pared down. <br><br>For someone who loves lots of emotional drama, it was right up my alley even if some of the things were a bit cliché. It wasn't bad enough that I wanted to throw my kindle but SY did stir the pot up quite a bit. <br><br>Of course, I loved the epilogue. I really think that should be a requirement unless the story is ongoing. Cam and Jo were perfect for each other and I just LOVED how Jo took care of Cole but especially when Cole did as well. <br><br><b>
  <i>"Baby, I already have taken on a teenage boy. I spend just as much time with the kid as I spend with you. He’s a good lad. I love him. I love you both."</i>
</b><br><br><br>Favorite quotes:<br><br>♥ "You and I are starting over today. I’m not some asshole who has judged you over and over again and got you wrong every single time."<br><br>♥ "A key: the way to a woman’s heart."<br><br>♥ "Perfectly good sex?" Cam interrupted us, drawing both our gazes. His voice was low with some unnamed emotion. "Abstain?" His now heated eyes ran the length of me before returning to meet mine. "Then <i>he</i> isn’t doing it right."<br><br>♥ "When I first saw you, I wanted you like I’d never wanted anyone. When you first tore me a new one, I wanted to know you. And when I got to know you, when I stood across a kitchen and you told me not to kill a spider because it didn’t say much for us as a species if we killed something because we feared it, I knew. I knew that I would never meet anyone as beautiful or as compassionate or as determined. I’ve known for a while that I was in love with you, Jo."<br><br>♥ "It’s almost debilitating. It’s too much. It’s … I can’t even describe it, but being with you is … there’s this intensity inside me all the time, this … constant pull, desperation … it’s like you’re branded on me or something. And it bloody well burns."</span>
  <a data-text-id="1906844678059608349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_620199148" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/620199148" />
    <a title="Auntee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886675-auntee"><img alt="Auntee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1281897695p2/886675.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/620199148?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Auntee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Auntee" href="/user/show/886675-auntee">Auntee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of &quot;On Dublin Street&quot; and anyone who likes a steamy, emotional read</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=made_me_cry">made_me_cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=2013_reads">2013_reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer620199148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10694085112155096732"><b>Samantha Young is the real deal...</b><br/><br/>One of the signs of a good writer (to me) is when you can take a character who I was not that thrilled with in a previous work, and make me fall in love with them in your latest. And that is what Samantha Young has done with the character of Jo Walker. In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15760001.On_Dublin_Street__On_Dublin_Street___1_' title='On Dublin Street (On Dublin Street, #1) by Samantha Young' rel='nofollow noopener'>On Dublin Street</a> I wasn't all that thrilled with her (even though I was sure there had to be a story about why she was such a slut looking for her next Sugar Daddy). I know there were some hints about her past,</span>
  <span id="freeText10694085112155096732" style="display:none"><b>Samantha Young is the real deal...</b><br><br>One of the signs of a good writer (to me) is when you can take a character who I was not that thrilled with in a previous work, and make me fall in love with them in your latest. And that is what Samantha Young has done with the character of Jo Walker. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15760001.On_Dublin_Street__On_Dublin_Street___1_" title="On Dublin Street (On Dublin Street, #1) by Samantha Young" rel="nofollow noopener">On Dublin Street</a> I wasn't all that thrilled with her (even though I was sure there had to be a story about why she was such a slut looking for her next Sugar Daddy). I know there were some hints about her past, but I had no idea how crappy it was, and after reading just a few chapters of "Down London Road", I forgave her for everything (even hitting on Braden!) and totally <i>understood</i> why she acted the way she did. Poor Jo, what she had to deal with...some of it brought tears to my eyes.<br><br><i>Jo...</i><br><a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/user/aunteecr/media/books/96eb123d-36ec-4a3a-a299-05aed75d30f7_zps9f106b73.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422282i/839933.jpg" alt=" photo 96eb123d-36ec-4a3a-a299-05aed75d30f7_zps9f106b73.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So, when Jo meets the hero of the book, Cameron,(who comes to work at Club 39 as a bartender) and he is a judgmental ass to her at first, I wanted to kick his arrogant butt!:) Ooh, I was pretty peeved at him for a while. But once they worked their issues out, and decided to be 'friends', I sure did enjoy the sparks and the smokin' chemistry they had, and it was a pure delight watching them fall in love. (oh my, the sex scenes....sooo <i>steamy</i> and emotional too) Cam was so <i>good</i> for Jo and her low self-esteem...granted, he's no Braden, and he could be obtuse at times, but I still <i>loved</i> him.<br><br><br><i>Cam...</i><a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/user/aunteecr/media/books/79845518-8dad-49df-a03a-c0ffb1fe0a33_zps0539cce0.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422282i/839934.jpg" alt=" photo 79845518-8dad-49df-a03a-c0ffb1fe0a33_zps0539cce0.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>I absolutely loved seeing Joss and Braden again (can't get enough of them), and enjoyed Jo's young brother Cole (future book a bit down the line?), and loved meeting all the new characters, especially <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Jo's cousin Olivia, who may have her own book with Cam's best friend Nate <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><i>Hi Braden!</i><br><a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/user/aunteecr/media/books/39e2635b-bd0f-4062-93e7-faea4aaeb8e5_zps273149ae.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422282i/839935.jpg" alt=" photo 39e2635b-bd0f-4062-93e7-faea4aaeb8e5_zps273149ae.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>What I'm most pleased about is that I found a new favorite author. I think this lady could write a phone book and manage to touch my heart. Her characters just seem to come alive--you feel like you know them and how they will react--and with her words she gets you so wrapped up in the story that you never want it to end! I've got no complaints about this one--it was one sexy, emotional ride. 5 highly recommended stars!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10694085112155096732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_609131275" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/609131275" />
    <a title="Steph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4215697-steph"><img alt="Steph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346102450p2/4215697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/609131275?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph" href="/user/show/4215697-steph">Steph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17280468-down-london-road">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4215697-steph?shelf=kindle-read">kindle-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer609131275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10315714485255347883"> Okay, I am going to try and keep this review nice and short because I don't want it to turn into me just ranting about the things I didn't like.<br/><br/> <b>The writing was wonderful, as usual with Samantha Young.</b><br/><br/> I really liked On Dublin Street, and have enjoyed other books by this author too. So I think I was expecting Down London Road to blow me away, but I was sadly disappointed.<br/><br/> I don't like it when people say they didn't like a book, but then doesn't give any reasons why, it annoys me. So here are my</span>
  <span id="freeText10315714485255347883" style="display:none"> Okay, I am going to try and keep this review nice and short because I don't want it to turn into me just ranting about the things I didn't like.<br /><br /> <b>The writing was wonderful, as usual with Samantha Young.</b><br /><br /> I really liked On Dublin Street, and have enjoyed other books by this author too. So I think I was expecting Down London Road to blow me away, but I was sadly disappointed.<br /><br /> I don't like it when people say they didn't like a book, but then doesn't give any reasons why, it annoys me. So here are my reasons...<br /> <br /> I never connected with Johanna's charcter, I didn't like her in the beginning at all. I understand that she needs money, but just go out and get a damn job like the rest of us. Oh wait, she already has two jobs. What kinda money is this woman after? A cool million? Welcome to the real world. We don't all get to be rich, we do the best we can and live within our means.<br /> She's always moaning that she has nothing going for her; the only way she can get by in life is by using her looks to her advantage. <i>*gags*</i><br /> I don't like the way she always goes for rich men, pretends to be this other person, gets them to like her and to buy her all these gifts, then she just sells them all on eBay. It just felt really dirty, and I didn't like it at all. No matter how bad she needs the money, it's horrible.<br /> She really annoyed me with her idiotic pride. <i>You'd rather be deceptive, and dirty to get your money, than accept a good job from a friend? What a moron!</i><br /><br /> Cameron was really great at times, but I didn't like the way he judges people, before he's even spoken to them. <br /> He's sexy and sweet and fun. But he's also a bit of a dick at times. The way he handled the Blair situation made me want to punch him in the face.<br /> <i>Oh, she came onto me. I pushed her away, but said she could stay over, have a shower and wear my t-shirt to bed. I can't believe you have a problem with this, Jo.</i><br /> What the hell... I would have kicked you in the balls, and then beat the shit out of her too. It was ridiculous.<br /><br /> They were pretty cheesy together. I had more than a few eye rolls.<br /><br /> There wasn't really a story line at all. Bar her dad coming back for like two pages.<br /> <br /> I get that her mum is a complete bitch, and that her childhood was pretty rough. But I just felt like she was using her past as an excuse...<br /> <i>I can't get a good job like normal people because my daddy made my self-esteem really low. I can't move out and get my own place because my drunken mother won't allow it.</i><br /> Blah blah blah. Just suck it up and make something of your life, lady.<br /><br /> Oh god, see I'm ranting now. Moving on...<br /> <br /> I absolutely adored seeing Braden, and the dinners at Elodie's were the real highlights of this book. <br /> But again, Joss seemed completely different. Like her personality had shifted into another person. It was weird.<br /><br /> Anyway, I will definitely read the next book in the series, because I know this author is capable of amazing things. But I won't be reading this book ever again.</span>

<div id="review_497544693" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/497544693" />
    <a title="La-Lionne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11644154-la-lionne"><img alt="La-Lionne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458815714p2/11644154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/497544693?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="La-Lionne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="La-Lionne" href="/user/show/11644154-la-lionne">La-Lionne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=badly-written">badly-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=just-blah">just-blah</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=skipped-a-lot">skipped-a-lot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=alpha-male-wannabe">alpha-male-wannabe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=frustrating">frustrating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=disappointing-sequel">disappointing-sequel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=returned-for-refund">returned-for-refund</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer497544693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4062966394092913799">I'm in shock. I can't believe I'm giving two stars to a book written by the same author who wrote On Dublin Street, which was one of my favorites of 2012. I still can't quite rap my head around it. <br/><br/>This book was nothing like On Dublin Street. I don't mean that I expected for stories to be similar or anything, I expected to be left with the same feelings I had after I read ODS: happiness, good kind of frustration, maybe a little of sadness or heartache. After finishing this one I was left with on</span>
  <span id="freeText4062966394092913799" style="display:none">I'm in shock. I can't believe I'm giving two stars to a book written by the same author who wrote On Dublin Street, which was one of my favorites of 2012. I still can't quite rap my head around it. <br /><br />This book was nothing like On Dublin Street. I don't mean that I expected for stories to be similar or anything, I expected to be left with the same feelings I had after I read ODS: happiness, good kind of frustration, maybe a little of sadness or heartache. After finishing this one I was left with only irritation, disbelieve and disappointment. And that are not feelings I'm looking for to be left with after reading a book.<br /><br />So here are the issues that I had:<br /><br /> - Jo. What is she about? I kind of get it what author was trying to create. Big sister trying to look after her brother and her alcoholic mother, who is absolute nightmare to have. She is struggling to provide for them working two jobs, stressing out of her mind. She dates only rich men, as an investment into her family's future (?). Her friends describes her as the strongest person they know. With a family situation like that, you have to be though as a nail. I get the idea. <br /><br />* * * WARNING SPOILERS!!! * * *<br /><br />Here is my problems with her character. Getting herself off while having sex with her boyfriend and thinking about Cam. Not all right! I get it. Author was trying to show her attraction to him. But do you have to push it that far? Not only I didn't find that hot or what ever, I actually thought it was kind of repulsing. Her certain parts were constantly tingling, panties vibrating in excitement (What?). I get it, Jo, you think he's hot, but pull yourself together and calm down will ya? <br /><br />I didn't get why was she dating rich men. She didn't came across as a gold digger. She never asked for anything from them. Yes, she never said no to their gifts, but never asked for anything either. She never cared about any of them, there was no love. She admitted that she wasn't herself around them and they never knew the real her. Even her friends said that her constantly fake giggling around Malcolm, was most annoying thing ever. So why waist time then?<br /><br />Then, there was the morning after, after she and he finally got together and did the thingy. She jumps out of bed and says "OMG we have to tell everybody that we are together." Are you freaking kidding me? You've known him for couple of weeks!!!! She knows half of rats a$$ about who he is, she doesn't know if relationship will ever work, but starts stressing out about telling people right away. All other guys, who she was dating for substantial amount of time, never got to see either her brother or her mother. And she was actually planning on marrying them if they would have asked. That just doesn't make any sense. <br /><br />Then there was a scene where she quit her job and ran home to blame it on Cam, but ended up blaming on PMS. Completely unnecessary drama.<br /><br />She was jealous of his ex-gilfriend, that he was with TEN YEARS AGO AND WHO SHE NEVER MET, only because he USED to be in love with her, and he haven't said I love you to her, yet! Oh Lord! <br /><br />- Cam. I kind of liked him at first. His background story was alright. I thought he was being sweet when he offered a key to Cole, and meaning behind his tattoo was interesting. But one character doesn't make a story, plus, later he screwed up big time. Jo was calling him possessive caveman. I have read quite a few books with possessive men, and Cam is not even a little bit it.<br /><br />- Story line. A complete mess. First half of the book dragged for ever, and after they got together hundred things started happening at once. She stressed so much to meet his parents, but when she finally did, all we got was "It was lovely, nice people, accepted her and Cole, his father loved her." We only got few lines of dialog the day after, something about freaking pancakes.<br /><br />Then, Cam digs up her long lost uncle and his daughter. Ok, let the drama begin, I thought. No, they met, talked, apologized, met Cole. That reunion didn't feel like big deal at all. It should have. Then uncle Mick went to meet her mother. Again I thought, uh-oh, put your safety helmets on, people. I imagined her crawling out of her room cussing everybody or maybe even throwing things. What do you know, she came out all decent (?) looking, showered, hair blow-dried, exchanged few sentences and went back to her room. I thought maybe that will be a turning point for her. Nope. She went to her old ways, drinking herself into oblivion and being angry, after Mick left. What's the point of all of it then???? <br /><br />Later, after having a little steamy somethin' with Jo in changing room, they bumped into Blair, his ex from ages ago. Of course Jo went blue with jealousy. Cam, the great guy that he is, asks for her phone number so they can catch up sometimes. OMG! Jo had some kind of telepathic conversation with Blair.<br /><br /><b>"I resent you, she said. I think I hate you, I replied. He was mine first, she answered. He is mine now, I growled."</b><br />Seriously??!!<br /><br />Now Jo is walking around all pissy. She comes to his place to talk about it, but ends up having gazillion orgasms. Ge goes on about that meeting Blair was just what he needed, about having a party next week and inviting Blair to catch up (??????!!!!!!). Afters fog wears off she wants to talk again, she thinks "Tell him! Ask him!". But when Cam asks "You ok?" she says "I'm fine. Just tired.".*GROWL*<br />But wait, she thinks it's not okay for him to keep in touch with his ex, but it is fine for her to keep texting Malcolm! I mean came on!!!<br /><br />I was determend to finish the book, but that last part seriously got on my nerve, I decided to DNF before I gave myself a stroke. 79% was more than enough, returning for refund. I wonder if in those last 21% was an explanation for the book title... I will never know.<br /><br />I did not like the story, at all. Confusing story line with no structure or clear direction to where story was heading, and all over the place characters.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12643850749854759850">This was an adult contemporary romance story featuring Jo from On Dublin Street.<br/><br/>I liked Jo in this and I felt bad for her at the way she was living her life in fear of her parents. It wasn’t fair the way she had to work 2 jobs and look after her younger brother all the time because of her mother’s alcoholism, but trying to hide what she was living with wasn’t doing her any favours either.<br/><br/> The storyline in this was about Jo meeting Cameron and them both feeling attracted to one another even thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText12643850749854759850" style="display:none">This was an adult contemporary romance story featuring Jo from On Dublin Street.<br /><br />I liked Jo in this and I felt bad for her at the way she was living her life in fear of her parents. It wasn’t fair the way she had to work 2 jobs and look after her younger brother all the time because of her mother’s alcoholism, but trying to hide what she was living with wasn’t doing her any favours either.<br /><br /> The storyline in this was about Jo meeting Cameron and them both feeling attracted to one another even though they were both with other people. Cameron was quite rude to Jo at the start though, and it took a while for him to be nice to her. The story was interesting though, and held my attention pretty well, and it was nice to catch up with Joss and Ellie from On Dublin street as well. <br /><br />The ending to this was pretty good, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and I just hope that Jo’s father stays away from her and her brother.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />7 out of 10<br /></span>

<div id="review_1723780439" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1723780439" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1723780439?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1723780439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11366719763760812409"><b>WARNING</b>: This review kind of sucks, mainly because I find it difficult to write reviews for romance books but enjoy. <br/><br/><i>Down London Road</i> was a book I went into expecting not to really like. I hadn't enjoyed <i>On Dublin Street</i> very much, from what I can remember. So, with my low expectations, I found I actually really enjoy <i>Down London Road</i>. <br/><br/>This book is able to be read as a standalone, but, of course, mentions characters from the first book but kind of makes you feel as if you <b>have</b> to read the first </span>
  <span id="freeText11366719763760812409" style="display:none"><b>WARNING</b>: This review kind of sucks, mainly because I find it difficult to write reviews for romance books but enjoy. <br /><br /><i>Down London Road</i> was a book I went into expecting not to really like. I hadn't enjoyed <i>On Dublin Street</i> very much, from what I can remember. So, with my low expectations, I found I actually really enjoy <i>Down London Road</i>. <br /><br />This book is able to be read as a standalone, but, of course, mentions characters from the first book but kind of makes you feel as if you <b>have</b> to read the first book. However, I found myself being completely in love with the characters and even remembering their dynamics from the first book. <br /><br />Now onto Amber's crappy book description:<br /><br /><b>Johanna</b> was the kind of character who you couldn't help but love, and considering the perspective of the book is hers. Johanna hasn't had the easiest life. Her dad was abusive, her mum checked out and she was left to care for her family. So, she dropped out of school at 16, got a job and proceeded to support her mother and brother. I admired Jo and her go-getter attitude. In no way did I judge her either for dating primarily rich guys, you do what you have to do in these situations. So, Jo's life is going pretty well for once and she thinks she may have finally found a guy she can settle down with when <b>Cam</b> comes into her life and throw her into a spin. Of course, this book is primarily focusing on the romance, but I found it interesting to see how Jo grew through the book. It was some phenomenal character development. <br /><br /><i>Characters</i><br /><br /><b>Johanna</b> had some crazy development. She started as a character who needed to take care of her family. A character who was ashamed by what she had to do and was incredibly self-conscious. Her development to a strong character who stands up for herself and doesn't let people treat her like trash or a gold digger, was amazing. I felt like it was slow and we really got time to watch each stage of Jo as she grew. <br /><br />I loved her loyalty to her brother as well. That was probably my favourite part about the book. The overall relationship between the two siblings. Sometimes in books like this siblings get pushed to the back and forgotten, but her brother Cole was front and centre for a majority of the book. <br /><br /><b>Cameron</b> was a character who annoyed me in the beginning. I found him judgmental and I kinda wanted to hit him, I wouldn't have blamed Jo if she had. I enjoyed learning about him and how he changed his treatment towards Jo, however, I wish we got the chance to learn more about him. It felt like we were sort of deprived of some information of him, considering he was theorised to have such a great life, especially when compared to Jo. <br /><br />I was frustrated at Cam though with the whole <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Becca situation <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. From someone who has incredibly little relationship experience but has read a lot of books <b>communication is key people.</b><br /><br /><i>Plot</i><br /><br />The plot, as I mentioned before, was focused primarily on the romance - however, the development of the romance was well done and beautiful. I enjoyed it. The plot also focuses on how Jo changes in the book and how she decides to stand for herself in the end. I mean, she does stay in a relationship without a break, which I kind of wish she had had, but I still enjoyed it incredibly. <br /><br /><i>Writing</i><br /><br />The writing was brilliant. Samatha Young wove words together to create a beautiful and heartfelt tale. I found myself wanting to cry for the characters in certain situations and getting mad at others - something that doesn't happen too often with books for me these days that I got a little more judgmental. <br /><br /><i>Overall</i><br /><br />Overall, I had some problems with this book, mainly <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the cheating that seemed to play a large part and the ex-partners making reappearances. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Despite these problems this book was an adorable and fast paced read that will warm your heart. It was super cute and quite fluffy but if you don't like cheating I would not recommend it for you. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11366719763760812409" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3463207389?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookadmirer " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookadmirer " href="/user/show/103293496-bookadmirer">Bookadmirer </a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3463207389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12161896147545346197">It's a decent book, nothing espectecular or anything.<br/><br/>What confused me is Johanna and Jocelyn friendship. In the first book Johanna flirted with Braden few times. And I recall Jocelyn wasn't very fond of her. She was portrayed as a <b>Gold Digger.</b> But in this book, they are best friend, Johanna is attending lunch with Jocelyn with Bradens family. On top of that she is also friends with Ellie and Hannah. I mean isn't it a bit odd? I mean I understand she is a heroine now but changing her character co</span>
  <span id="freeText12161896147545346197" style="display:none">It's a decent book, nothing espectecular or anything.<br /><br />What confused me is Johanna and Jocelyn friendship. In the first book Johanna flirted with Braden few times. And I recall Jocelyn wasn't very fond of her. She was portrayed as a <b>Gold Digger.</b> But in this book, they are best friend, Johanna is attending lunch with Jocelyn with Bradens family. On top of that she is also friends with Ellie and Hannah. I mean isn't it a bit odd? I mean I understand she is a heroine now but changing her character completely and making huge changes like this is too much for me.<br /><br />Also, it turns out Jocelyn isn't a <b>Gold Digger.</b> She was with rich boyfriends because they gave her a sense of safety? She worked hard for the money she earned and only takes gifts from her rich boyfriends. Is it a joke? Because that's what I felt.<br /><br />The romance was actually very good. Cameron was a bit judgemental towards Johanna but I kind of get why. Cameron's bond with Cole is also very cute. If I didn't read earlier books I might enjoyed it more because those stuff won't bother me. It's not that I didn't enjoy it. But lots of thing felt ridiculous to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12161896147545346197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zIw4cUZvGUTZrRUuZnYhlz3Jwxa6/PwVtSqhMbQIy0kSgfMf4qHgPcCNgNDomdkTOWLA65Tz63BI5bBIKVzZSA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IPP+SgdoD+MPBwQzn5/Ds2iFLCuGVDwgQ0lY9+4QT9n+/jUko6b2mhYnkc0RcDs3bC4v1qhbK0W+hkmOc0Rd2A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer14826746859454758974">Samantha Young is a New York Times, USA Today and Wall Street Journal bestselling author from Stirlingshire, Scotland. She's been nominated for several Goodreads Choice Awards. She writes adult contemporary and paranormal romance, YA urban fantasy and YA contemporary fiction. Currently published in 30 countries, Samantha is a #1 international bestselling author. <br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/></span>
